This can\\n42:   // occur in two ways.  Firstly, a node may be created during legalization but\\n43:   // never passed to the legalization core.  This is usually due to the implicit\\n44:   // folding that occurs when using the DAG.getNode operators.  Secondly, a new\\n45:   // node may be passed to the legalization core, but when analyzed may morph\\n46:   // into a different node, leaving the original node as a NewNode in the DAG.\\n47:   // A node may morph if one of its operands changes during analysis.  Whether\\n48:   // it actually morphs or not depends on whether, after updating its operands,\\n49:   // it is equivalent to an existing node: if so, it morphs into that existing\\n50:   // node (CSE).  An operand can change during analysis if the operand is a new\\n51:   // node that morphs, or it is a processed value that was mapped to some other\\n52:   // value (as recorded in ReplacedValues) in which case the operand is turned\\n53:   // into that other value.  If a node morphs then the node it morphed into will\\n54:   // be used instead of it for legalization, however the original node continues\\n55:   // to live on in the DAG.\\n56:   // The conclusion is that though there may be nodes marked NewNode in the DAG,\\n57:   // all uses of such nodes are also marked NewNode: the result is a fungus of\\n58:   // NewNodes growing on top of the useful nodes, and perhaps using them, but\\n59:   // not used by them.\\n60: \\n61:   // If a value is mapped by ReplacedValues, then it must have no uses, except\\n62:   // by nodes marked NewNode (see above).\\n63: \\n64:   // The final node obtained by mapping by ReplacedValues is not marked NewNode.\\n65:   // Note that ReplacedValues should be applied iteratively.\\n66: \\n67:   // Note that the ReplacedValues map may also map deleted nodes (by iterating\\n68:   // over the DAG we never dereference deleted nodes).  This means that it may\\n69:   // also map nodes marked NewNode if the deallocated memory was reallocated as\\n70:   // another node, and that new node was not seen by the LegalizeTypes machinery\\n71:   // (for example because it was created but not used). \\n82:     /// Returns the EVT that represents a vector EC.Min elements in length,\\n83:     /// where each element is of type VT.\\n84:     static EVT getVectorVT(LLVMContext &Context, EVT VT, /// bitwidth.\\n94:     EVT changeVectorElementTypeToInteger() const {\\n95:       if (isSimple())\\n96:         return getSimpleVT().changeVectorElementTypeToInteger();\\n97:       return For example, implementing i8 arithmetic in an\\n12: // i32 register (often needed on powerpc).\\n13: // Expansion is the act of changing a computation in an illegal type into a\\n14: // computation in two identical registers of a smaller type.  For example,\\n15: // implementing i64 arithmetic in two i32 registers (often needed on 32-bit\\n16: // targets).\\n17: //\\n18: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\n19: \\n20: #include \\\"LegalizeTypes.h\\\"\\n21: #include \\\"llvm/Analysis/TargetLibraryInfo.h\\\"\\n22: #include \\\"llvm/CodeGen/StackMaps.h\\\"\\n23: #include \\\"llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h\\\"\\n24: #include \\\"llvm/IR/DerivedTypes.h\\\"\\n25: #include \\\"llvm/IR/DiagnosticInfo.h\\\"\\n26: #include \\\"llvm/Support/ErrorHandling.h\\\"\\n27: #include \\\"llvm/Support/KnownBits.h\\\"\\n28: #include \\\"llvm/Support/raw_ostream.h\\\"\\n29: #include <algorithm>\\n30: using namespace llvm;\\n31: \\n32: #define DEBUG_TYPE \\\"legalize-types\\\"\\n33: \\n34: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\n35: //  Integer Result Promotion\\n36: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\n37: \\n38: /// PromoteIntegerResult - This method is called when a result of a node is\\n39: /// found to be in need of promotion to a larger type.  At this point, the node\\n40: /// may also have invalid operands or may have other results that need\\n41: /// expansion, we just know that (at least) one result needs promotion.\\n42: void DAGTypeLegalizer::PromoteIntegerResult(SDNode *N, unsigned ResNo) {\\n43:   LLVM_DEBUG(dbgs() << \\\"Promote integer result: \\\"; N->dump(&DAG));\\n44:   SDValue Res = SDValue();\\n45: \\n46:   // See if the target wants to custom expand this node.\\n47:   if (CustomLowerNode(N, N->getValueType(ResNo), true)) {\\n48:     LLVM_DEBUG(dbgs() << \\\"Node has been custom expanded, done\\\\n\\\");\\n49:     return;\\n50:   }\\n51: \\n52:   switch (N->getOpcode()) {\\n53:   default:\\n54: #ifndef NDEBUG\\n55:     dbgs() << \\\"PromoteIntegerResult #\\\" << ResNo << \\\": \\\";\\n56:     N->dump(&DAG); dbgs() << \\\"\\\\n\\\";\\n57: #endif\\n58:     report_fatal_error(\\\"Do not know how to promote this operator!\\\");\\n59:   case ISD::MERGE_VALUES:Res = PromoteIntRes_MERGE_VALUES(N, ResNo); break;\\n60:   case ISD::AssertSext:  Res = PromoteIntRes_AssertSext(N); break;\\n61:   case ISD::AssertZext:  Res = PromoteIntRes_AssertZext(N); break;\\n62:   case ISD::BITCAST:     Res = PromoteIntRes_BITCAST(N); break;\\n63:   case ISD::VP_BITREVERSE:\\n64:   case ISD::BITREVERSE:  Res = PromoteIntRes_BITREVERSE(N); break;\\n65:   case ISD::VP_BSWAP:\\n66:   case ISD::BSWAP:       Res = PromoteIntRes_BSWAP(N); break;\\n67:   case ISD::BUILD_PAIR:  Res = PromoteIntRes_BUILD_PAIR(N); break;\\n68:   case ISD::Constant:    Res = PromoteIntRes_Constant(N); break;\\n69:   case ISD::VP_CTLZ_ZERO_UNDEF:\\n70:   case ISD::VP_CTLZ:\\n71:   case ISD::CTLZ_ZERO_UNDEF:\\n72:   case ISD::CTLZ:        Res = PromoteIntRes_CTLZ(N); break;\\n73:   case ISD::CTLS:        Res = PromoteIntRes_CTLS(N);
